MTA Wiki
RoutesCorridorsProjects

project

Fordham Road – Inwood Bus Priority

project_fordham-rd-bus-priority

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

[fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

[fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

[fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

[fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

[fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

Outreach And ABLE Evaluation

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. After March 2022, the project was put on hold while DOT and MTA established a six-month ABLE camera evaluation, conducted Arthur Avenue surveys, and continued discussions with institutions and stakeholders. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p013_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p014_c0005]

ABLE was implemented on Bx12 SBS on November 18, 2022 with a 60-day warning period. The June 2023 deck says nearly 16,000 tickets were issued on Fordham Road between Sedgwick Avenue and Southern Boulevard from November 18, 2022 to April 21, 2023; the same page reports April 2023 buses 4.7% faster, but still slower than the 2008 post-SBS benchmark of 6.7 mph. DOT and MTA concluded that ABLE had a positive effect, but enforcement alone had not restored prior speeds because blockages remained frequent. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p024_c0005] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p025_c0002]

Preferred Direction

As of the May and June 2023 materials, DOT and MTA were advancing Alternative A, offset bus lanes, rather than a busway. The June CB6 deck says Alternative A was selected based on traffic-analysis factors and community concerns because it was expected to improve bus speeds, reliability, and curb demand while minimizing effects on north-south bus corridors. It also says the design would add about 150 parking/loading spaces corridor-wide, about 50 in CB6, while noting that offset lanes are not foolproof because double parking can still block the lane. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p049_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p051_c0004]

The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p052_c0005]

Project Scope

Fordham Road-Inwood Bus Priority was presented as a Fordham Road and Bx12 corridor bus-priority study, with the University Heights Bridge and 207th Street connection treated as part of the problem area. The March 2022 CAB deck said the Community Advisory Board would guide the project before, during, and after implementation, and that DOT was presenting three design alternatives for study and feedback. The same deck framed the need around the Bx12 as the busiest Bronx bus route, 85,000 average daily riders on five routes, a major Bronx-Manhattan connection, and corridor households with low private-vehicle access. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p004_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p007_c0002]

The operational problem was not just that Fordham Road already had bus lanes. The sources say existing curbside bus lanes were frequently blocked, curb demand was growing, and Bx12-SBS speeds were slowest westbound from Boston Road to Broadway/Isham Street and eastbound from 207th Street/Broadway to Boston Road. The University Heights Bridge segment was called one of the slowest parts of the route, with westbound bus speeds below 4 mph and eastbound speeds around 6-8 mph. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p008_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p010_c0004] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p011_c0005]

Alternatives Studied

In March 2022, DOT said it was conducting traffic analysis for three bus-priority alternatives along the Bx12 corridor. Alternative A would convert existing curbside lanes on Fordham Road into offset bus lanes, with offset or curbside bus lanes also explored on 207th Street from 10th Avenue through the University Heights Bridge. Alternative B would restrict eastbound through traffic on Fordham Road from Morris Avenue to Webster Avenue except for buses and trucks. Alternative C would apply busway restrictions in both directions, while keeping curb access for loading and keeping Alternative A bus lanes outside the busway section. [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p024_c0003] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p025_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p026_c0006] [fordham_rd_inwood_cab_mar2022#p027_c0006]

By the May and June 2023 decks, DOT described a completed traffic-analysis framework: counts at more than 60 intersections, origin-destination analysis using anonymized GPS or connected-vehicle data, intersection modeling, in-person validation, and scenarios that assumed up to a 40% volume reduction. The June CB6 deck says the reported alternative results assumed about 20% of vehicles would travel at another time, use another mode, or take a road outside the modeled network. [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p027_c0002] [fordham_rd_inwood_cb6_jun2023#p036_c0003]

The 2023 materials describe a long outreach record, including 2019 merchant and shopper surveys, 2020 public polling, CAB meetings, a 2021 public workshop, stakeholder briefings, and June 2023 community-board presentations. The documented next steps were source-time plans, not proof of completion: June 2023 community-board presentations, summer 2023 design refinement and feedback, and fall 2023 planned implementation.
